25:T392b,<entryFree id="n22809" key="شَكَرَ لَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">شَكَرَ لَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَهُ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, K,) but the former is the more chaste, (S,) and the latter is for <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ نِعْمَتَهُ</foreign>, (A,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">شَكُرَ</orth>
                  </form>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرَانٌ</foreign> (S, A, * Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">شُكُورٌ</foreign>, (S, K) which last, in the Kur lxxvi. 9, may be either an inf. n. or pl. of <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> [used as a simple subst.], (S,) <hi rend="ital">He thanked him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">praised, eulogized,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commended, him, for a benefit</hi> or <hi rend="ital">benefits:</hi> (S:) <hi rend="ital">he was grateful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thankful, to him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he acknowledged his beneficence,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">spoke of it largely:</hi> (S, *  K: [but in the S, the verb in the former sense has <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> only for its inf. n., and it is implied that in the latter sense it has for its inf. n. only <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرَانٌ</foreign>, as will be seen below:]) and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ لِلّٰهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>, (Lh, Msb, K,) which latter is less common than the former, and even disallowed by As in prose, though allowed by him in verse, (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ بِٱللّٰهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ نِعْمَةَ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ بِنِعْمَةِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, (Lh, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ لِلّٰهِ نِعْمَتَهُ</foreign>, (A,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرَانٌ</foreign> (Msb) [and <foreign lang="ar">شُكُورٌ</foreign>], <hi rend="ital">He thanked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">praised, God for his beneficence:</hi> (A:) <hi rend="ital">he was grateful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thankful, to God;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acknowledged his beneficence,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">spoke of it largely:</hi> (K:) <hi rend="ital">he acknowledge the beneficence of God, and acted in the manner incumbent on him in rendering Him obedience and abstaining from disobedience;</hi> so that <foreign lang="ar">شُكْر</foreign> is in word and in deed: (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22809-1" target="تَشَكَّرَ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لَهُ</foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ لَهُ</foreign>: (S, A, Msb, K:) you say, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22809-2" target="تَشَكَّرْتُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لَهُ مَا صَنَعَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thanked him, &amp;c., for what he did</hi>]: (A:) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22809-3" target="تشكّر" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n22812"/>لَهُ بَلَآءَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He was grateful to Him, &amp;c.,</hi> i. e. to God, <hi rend="ital">for his probation</hi>]: (K:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَشْكُرُ إِلَيْكَ نِعَمَ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I praise to thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mention to thee with thanks, the favours of God</hi>]: (L in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign>:) [but there are many explanations of <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ</foreign> beside those given above: its meanings will be more fully shown by what here follows:] <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> is the <hi rend="ital">thanking</hi> a benefactor; or <hi rend="ital">praising, eulogizing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commending,</hi> him, (S, A,) <hi rend="ital">for a benefits:</hi> (S:) or the <hi rend="ital">being grateful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thankful;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acknowledging beneficence;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">speaking of it largely;</hi> and [in the copies of the K, “ or, ” but this is evidently a mistake,] <hi rend="ital">it is only on account of favour received;</hi> (K;) and <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرَانٌ</foreign> is [the same, being] <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُفْرَانٌ</foreign>: (S:) <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> [sometimes] differs from <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign>; (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign>;) for <foreign lang="ar">شكر</foreign> is only on account of favour received; whereas <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign> is sometimes because of favour received, (Th, Az, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign>, and Msb ubi suprà,) and sometimes form other causes; (Th ubi suprà;) [and thus] the latter is of more common application than the former; (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign>;) therefore you do not say <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرْتُهُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَجَاعَتِهِ</foreign>, but you say <foreign lang="ar">حَمِدْتُهُ على شجاعته</foreign>: (Msb ubi suprà:) or <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> is more common than <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign> with respect to its kinds and means, and more particular with respect to the objects to which it relates; and the latter is more common with respect to the objects to which it relates, and more particular with respect to the means; for the former is, with the heart, the <hi rend="ital">being humble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lowly, and submissive;</hi> and with the tongue, the act of <hi rend="ital">praising, eulogizing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commending;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">acknowledging beneficence;</hi> and with the members, the act of <hi rend="ital">obeying,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">submitting one's self;</hi> and the object to which it relates is the benefactor, exclusively of his essential qualities; therefore one does not say <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرْنَا ٱللّٰهَ عَلَى حَيَاتِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">we thanked God for his existence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">praised Him, &amp;c.</hi>]; but He is <foreign lang="ar">مَحْمُود</foreign> on that account, like as He is for his beneficence; and <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> is also for beneficence: thus <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign> relates to every object to which, as an object, <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> relates; but the reverse is not the case: and everything whereby is <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign>, thereby is <foreign lang="ar">شكر</foreign>; but the reverse is not the case; for the latter is by means of the members, or limbs, and the former is by means of the tongue: <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> is of three kinds; with the heart, or mind, which is the <hi rend="ital">forming an</hi> [<hi rend="ital">adequate</hi>] <hi rend="ital">idea of the benefit;</hi> and with the tongue, which is the <hi rend="ital">praising, eulogizing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commending, the benefactor;</hi> and with the members, or limbs, which is the <hi rend="ital">requiting the benefit according to its desert:</hi> it rests upon five foundations; humility of him who renders it towards him to whom it is rendered; his love of him; his acknowledgment of his benefit; the eulogizing him for it; and his not making use of the benefit in a manner which he [who has conferred it] dislikes: it is also explained as <hi rend="ital">devotion of the heart to love of the benefactor,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of the members to obey him,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the employment of the tongue in mentioning him and eulogizing him:</hi> [and there are several other explanations of it which it is unnecessary to add:] some say that it is formed by transposition from <foreign lang="ar">كَشْرٌ</foreign>, the “ act of uncovering, or exposing to view: ” others, that it is from <foreign lang="ar">عَيْنٌ شَكْرَى</foreign> “ a full fountain, or eye; ” accord. to which etymology it would signify the <hi rend="ital">being full of the praise of the benefactor.</hi> (B, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> on the part of God signifies <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  The <hi rend="ital">requiting and commending</hi> [a person]: (K:) or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  the <hi rend="ital">forgiving</hi> a man: or <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  the <hi rend="ital">regarding</hi> him <hi rend="ital">with content, satisfaction, good will,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">favour:</hi> and hence, necessarily, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  the <hi rend="ital">recompensing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rewarding,</hi> him: the saying <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ ٱللّٰهُ سَعْيَهُ</foreign> signifies <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">May God recompense,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reward, his work,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">labour.</hi> (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَكِرَتْ</foreign>, aor.

                  <foreign lang="ar">يَبْرُوح</foreign> [q. v.], <hi rend="ital">and smaller; having a white flower, and a slender stem, without any fruit; and its seed is like</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the</hi>
